196    In re-examination, Quah was asked to clarify the source of her monies to meet these two GIRO deductions (which had taken place on a monthly basis, together with other deductions). She failed to provide a direct answer:[^309]

> Q:    Mdm Quah, can I ask you to pick up tab 2 of the Agreed Bundle? And I would ask you to turn to page 205 and then turn over the page to 206. Now, on this page the Learned DPP had asked you about GIRO payment transactions recorded for 1st September 2010 and 3rd September 2010. Do you recall?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    Okay, can you clarify what was your source of monies to make these GIRO payments?

> Q:    This is DBS Cashline. I’ve been using this for many years. I have deposited my own personal money into this account. I could use the \[overdraft line\]…for other expenses of mine. But ---

> A:    Okay, Mdm Quah ---

> Q:    that’s it.

> Q:    is that your clarification?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    Okay.

> A:    Because it’s my own personal money inside.

197    I did not find Quah’s “clarification” persuasive. It was vague, and she failed to refer to her August-September 2010 bank statement (or any other statement for this account) to show the “personal money” she had apparently deposited into her Cashline Account to meet these GIRO deductions. A review of her bank statements for the Cashline Account showed that she was being charged interest nearly _every_ month from September 2010 to June 2014. While the total interest charged between this period was relatively small (amounting to $1,447.39), it was difficult to understand why Quah willingly paid such interest (as she said she did[^310]) nearly every month on sums she was borrowing from the bank to give to TSM – when:

> (a)     she was not going to retain any money for herself;

> (b)     her case was that she was never comfortable with TSM’s alleged instructions;[^311] and

> (c)     she could have deposited all the cash cheques into her Savings Account (which already existed) and not pay _any_ interest.

198    It was also not clear why it was “very troublesome” for Quah to queue and encash these cash cheques over the counter at the bank (and not pay any interest to the bank). After all, this was one of her duties as an employee.

Quah’s CashPlus Account (another credit line)

199    The bank statements for the CashPlus Account showed that Quah was depositing cash cheques into an account that was _perpetually_ in overdraft (a fact that she agreed to as well). But, she denied that it was illogical for her to pay interest in relation to _cash_ cheques that belonged to the Company. She then went to claim – again, for the _first_ time – that TSM had seen that her CashPlus and Cashline accounts had overdraft facilities, and so wanted her to deposit the cash cheques into these accounts as it would be easier for him to get the money. She also claimed (once more, for the _first_ time) that TSM would help her pay the interest that her two credit lines incurred as she was letting him use her accounts[^312] (a version that contradicted her earlier evidence that _she_ paid the interest incurred on the Cashline Account[^313]). I set out Quah’s evidence in detail, to show the many fresh claims she made during her cross-examination – none of which were raised during TSM’s cross-examination and in her examination-in-chief:[^314]

> Q:    …I want you to turn to AB4. Now, AB4 is your bank account statement for \[your CashPlus Account\]. And I just want you to look at the 1st page, so we’re at AB4 page 469…Are you there, Mdm Quah?

> A:    Yes \[as spoken by the Witness in English\].

> Q:    Now, there’s a line that says, “15th Jan ODINT charge”. Do you see that? In the middle of the page.

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    You will agree this stands for overdraft interest charge?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    In other words, you had withdrawn more from the bank than you had deposited?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, you owed the bank interest?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And in fact, \[your CashPlus Account\] was in overdraft all the way until it was closed on 19th April 2012?...

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, it was perpetually in overdraft?

> …

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And, again, this is one of the bank accounts that you said you deposited cash cheques into?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, again, you were paying interest on cash cheques belonging to \[the Company\]?

> A:    It’s not like this.

> Q:    Or you were depositing the cash cheques into an account that was perpetually in overdraft? Yes or no?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, you will agree with me that it’s illogical to pay interest on cash cheques that belonged to the company?

> Int:  “I disagree. Because \[TSM\] saw that I have \[overdraft\].”

> A:    Easier for him to take the money \[as spoken by Witness in English\].

> Int:  “I have OD bank.”

> Court:    She needs to keep her evidence in Mandarin.

> Int:  “My \[Cashline and CashPlus\] accounts both have \[overdraft\] interest. But \[TSM\] saw this and he wanted me to deposit the cash into this. So that it’s easier for him to take money.”

> A:    Anything happened \[as spoken by Witness in English\].

> Court:    In Chinese, please, Madam.

> A:    If there’s any problem, if there’s interest charge, sometimes \[TSM\] would help me to pay, sometimes, I will have to pay on my own. Because these 2 accounts have \[overdraft\], it will be easier for him to get the money. For those accounts…without \[overdraft\] line, he would not touch them.

> **Q:**      **Mdm Quah this very long and complicated explanation that you have just given – first time that you are giving this explanation. Yes? Yes or no?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> Q:    I’ll leave it as that. Now, without depositing cash cheques into \[your CashPlus and Cashline accounts you\] agree that the interest incurred would have been greater. Agree?

> A:    I disagree.

> Q:    That’s illogical, Mdm Quah.

> A:    Because I am in control of my own bank account. The reason I closed the \[CashPlus\] account \[was because TSM\] doesn’t want to have so many \[overdraft\] accounts for him to play around with. Because every time when I told him that there was \[overdraft interest\], I know that he would help me pay. Because I am letting him use my accounts. If there is no \[overdraft\] line, he wouldn’t touch them.

> **Q:**      **Alright, Mdm Quah, so now we have a brand-new explanation that \[TSM\], you let him use your accounts. That is what you just said. Agree or disagree?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> Q:    And you agree this make\[s\] no sense because these are actually your bank accounts?

> A:    He did look at my bank accounts. Every time I bank in cheques and I receive bank statements, I will need to show it to him. I did ask him to bank into his own account. He said he does not have an ATM card. I want\[ed\] him to use his own Maybank account to issue cheques to the 3 \[directors\]. And he said, “It’s troublesome. They wanted cash.”

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

200    I did not give _any_ weight to Quah’s belated claims. I also did not see any sense in Quah borrowing money from credit lines on a monthly basis – and paying interest to the banks in respect of money that would not even go to her (but to TSM, as she claimed). This was also in light of the fact that Quah had a Savings Account, into which she could have deposited _all_ the cash cheques and not incur any interest (assuming that TSM did indeed instruct her to deposit the cash cheques into her accounts). Indeed, if TSM had been “chasing after \[her\] for money all the time”[^315] (as Quah claimed he was), it would surely have been faster for Quah to queue and encash the cash cheques over the counter at the banks (and get the cash there and then). Looking at the whole of the evidence, I agreed with the Prosecution that Quah was using the cash cheques she deposited into her credit lines to pay off her own debts[^316] and for her personal expenses.[^317]

##### Quah kept monies from Ho’s personal cheque

201    It was Quah’s case that _all_ the withdrawals she listed in her Compilation pertained _only_ to the cash cheques she collected from EDS, Win Tran, and Time-Flex (which she later encashed by depositing into her personal accounts).[^318] In cross-examination, she was referred to a cash cheque that Ho had issued from his _personal_ account (and not the accounts of EDS or Win Tran). Dated 8 July 2011, this cheque was for the sum of $4,100.65.[^319] Quah agreed that she had encashed this cheque on 8 July 2011 by depositing it into her Cashline Account.[^320] When asked if she had withdrawn the full sum of $4,100.65 to hand over to TSM, she testified that she withdrew _only_ a total of $1,500 (_ie_, leaving a balance of $2,600.65 in her account) to give to TSM. She did not explain why she only withdrew this smaller sum. Neither did she adduce any documentary evidence showing that she did actually pass this smaller sum to TSM. On this note, I bore in mind her evidence that her Compilation only covered the cash cheques she collected from EDS, Win Tran, and Time-Flex. It did not cover cash cheques that Ho issued from his _personal_ account. Quah agreed with this as well in cross-examination:[^321]

> Q:    Alright, I’ll move on. Now, Mdm Quah, you can go with me to AB15.14? This is on page 708 of the bundle.

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And can you also pick up AB2 at page 239? Are you there with me, Mdm Quah?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So the cash cheque of \[$4,100.65\] from Eric Ho, you agree that you banked this sum into your \[Cashline Account\]?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And we can see that on page 239 \[of AB2\]?

> A:    Yes.

> **Q:**      **But you did not, in fact, withdraw cash amounting to \[$4,100.65\] so that you could hand over the sum to \[TSM\]?**

> **A:**      **I only…withdrew $1,500.** Okay, I did deposit this sum of money and when I withdrew it, I also similarly, withdrew 500 and 1,000 to \[give to\] him.

> …

> **Q:**      **But actually, if you look at the cheque on page 708 \[of AB15\], it’s a cheque from Eric Ho.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And we agreed that \[your Compilation\], it relates to cash cheques from EDS, Win Tran and Time-Flex?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> Q:    So a cash cheque from Eric Ho would fall outside the scope of \[your Compilation\], you agree?

> A:    Can I take a look at \[my Compilation\]?

> **Q:**      **You don’t actually need to take a look at the documents for this, Mdm Quah. So just listen to the questions. Now, we are agreed that \[your Compilation\] concerns cheques from EDS, Win Tran and Time-Flex \[and\] not from Eric Ho.**

> **A:**      **I agree**, but sometimes Eric Ho would use his own personal cheque to pay the company although it’s very seldom.

> **Q:**      **Okay. Well, we’re actually going by what you said. So this is really your evidence that \[your Compilation\]…only had to do with EDS, Win Tran and Time-Flex.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

202    Quah’s evidence thus amounted to an admission that she did keep more than half of the sum encashed from this cheque (assuming that she did actually hand $1,500 to TSM). In any event, I placed _no_ weight on her evidence that she handed $1,500 to TSM. She never explained why she did not pass the full sum to TSM. It was also not her evidence that she passed TSM only $1,500 because she had already given him the remainder using her own cash (as she belatedly testified in respect of another cheque from Win Tran[^322]). In this vein, her evidence was also inconsistent with her earlier testimony that TSM was “chasing after \[her\] for money all the time”.[^323] If this was not a case where she had given TSM her own cash in advance, why did she fail to give TSM – who was allegedly always ravenous for money – the full sum from this cheque? This was simply another instance of Quah encashing a cash cheque for her own use.

##### Quah diverted cash cheque into mother’s account

203    In examination-in-chief, Quah was referred to one of her responses in her fifth investigation statement.[^324] This related to a cash cheque from EDS, for $3,067.75.[^325] The cheque was dated 29 October 2010. Behind this cheque, Quah had written to instruct the bank to deposit the _full_ sum into her mother’s account. The relevant extract from her statement read as follows:[^326]

> 13.    The following question was posed by the \[IO\]:

>> Q21?   I am showing you the same document, a transaction dated 29 October 2010, amounting to S$3067.75 using cheque OCBC 887776 paid by \[EDS\]. I am also showing you the cheque image from OCBC 887776 dated 29 October 2010 amounting to S$3067.75 and the recipient is one, Ms Tan Ah Nya. Can you explain why Tan Ah Nya is the recipient of the amount of S$3067.75 \[instead of the Company\]?

>> Answer:    Tan Ah Nya is my mother. I wish to state that this is one of the transactions that I **divert** the cash cheque to my mother\[‘s\] account. I had informed \[TSM\] about it and I had also reimbursed it in cash to \[TSM\]. My mother is 84 years old and wheelchair bound, \[a\] heart patient \[with\] slight dementia. There is a maid looking after her. Her bank account is maintained by me. It means that I would withdraw the money for her expenses She did not withdraw the money. As and when there is a need for her expenses, I would withdraw for her by ATM.

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

204    Quah was then asked about her understanding of “divert”. She responded that she understood “divert” to mean “exchange”.[^327] In cross-examination, she stated that her statement should have stated “exchange” instead of “divert”.[^328] I was aware that the IO had testified that he did not clarify with Quah as to what she meant by her use of the word “divert”.[^329] However, it was never put to the IO that Quah had meant to use “exchange” instead of “divert” in her statement. In any event, I did not think that the IO had any reason to clarify the meaning of “divert” with Quah. This was in light of Quah’s clear proficiency in the English language.[^330] After all, she had informed the IO that her highest level of education was the GCE “A” Level and that she preferred to speak in English when her statements were recorded. The words “divert” and “exchange” are also very distinct in meaning. I found it difficult to understand how she could have been confused over their use. I was aware that Quah had claimed in her statement that:[^331]

> (a)     she had “informed” TSM about the diversion of this cash cheque into her mother’s account; and

> (b)     she had later “reimbursed” TSM the sum of $3,067.75 in cash.

205    However, these claims were never put to TSM. They were also inconsistent with Quah’s evidence that she had “no choice” but to give TSM her own money first because he was “chasing after \[her\] for money all the time”.[^332] If this were indeed the case, why would TSM permit Quah to first use the monies for her own purposes? I thus agreed with the Prosecution that this was “yet another clear instance of \[Quah\] treating the \[Entrusted Monies\] as her own”.[^333]

##### Quah’s fresh claims regarding monies in Joint Account

206    The joint account between Quah and her nephew was opened on 3 March 2014. She closed it in less than four months, on 27 June 2014. Quah’s transactions with this account from 31 March 2014 to 27 June 2014 appear in the following table:

align="left" class="r" rowspan="1" valign="top"><p align="justify" class="Table-Para-1">$1,118.74</p></td><td align="left" class="r" rowspan="1" valign="top"><p align="justify" align="justify" class="Table-Para-1">Closed</p></td></tr></tbody></table>

  
  

207    In cross-examination, Quah was referred to four cash cheques issued by EDS between March 2014 and May 2014:

class="Table-Para-1">$5,960.91</p></td><td align="left" class="" rowspan="1" valign="top"><p align="justify" class="Table-Para-1">Summation (<b>P26</b>), at S/No 65</p></td></tr></tbody></table>

  
  

208    Quah _agreed_ that she had received all of these cash cheques (amounting to a total of $20,145.41) from EDS, and that she had deposited them into the Joint Account (corresponding to the cheque deposits shown in the bank statement[^334]). She also _agreed_ that she did _not_ withdraw the sums she encashed on each occasion to give to TSM (neither were such withdrawals shown on the bank statement).[^335] The Prosecution then directed Quah to her withdrawal of $50,000 from the Joint Account _via_ a cashier’s order on 11 June 2014.[^336] It was Quah’s evidence that she had obtained this order on 11 June 2014 in her _own_ name, and then deposited it into her Savings Account later that same day.[^337]

209    According to Quah, she had previously lent cash of $11,000 and $40,000 (_ie_, a total of $51,000) to TSM on two different occasions. She claimed that $11,000 was “for Eric Ho’s deposit” as Ho pumped more than $10,000 worth of diesel every month. The Company thus required a larger deposit from Ho, for EDS’s supply of diesel to continue on credit terms. Quah did not explain why she had to extend the loan of $40,000 to TSM.

210    Quah claimed that the cashier’s order for $50,000 was “what \[TSM\] returned to \[her\]” for the $51,000 she had previously lent him. She testified that TSM was aware that she had been banking these cash cheques into the Joint Account. She also said that TSM had asked her to bring this cashier’s order to the Office “for him to see” after she obtained it from the bank. She claimed that TSM had then made a copy of it in the Office and written the words, “I did not owe you anymore” on the copy (which she said he then retained). The Prosecution then suggested to Quah that she never had $50,000 to lend to TSM, given that her two remaining accounts were both credit lines. Quah disagreed:[^338]

> Q:    Now, you claimed that you lent $50,000 to \[TSM\]?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    But out of \[the\] 3 personal bank accounts of yours…\[the CashPlus Account\] was always in overdraft…agree or disagree?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And \[the other account\] was \[the Cashline Account\]?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, I’m suggesting to you that you never had $50,000 to lend to \[TSM\]?

> A:    I disagree.

211    Assuming that TSM was indeed returning $50,000 to her, the Prosecution then asked Quah why there was a need to _transfer_ this sum from her Joint Account to her Savings Account. After all, Quah could simply have let this sum remain in her Joint Account. Quah responded that she had her own reasons for doing so, but did not elaborate.[^339] In re-examination, she testified that her nephew’s father had entrusted her with $40,000 before he died to fund the studies of her nephew (who was studying in a local polytechnic). According to Quah, $40,000 out of the $51,000 she had lent to TSM therefore belonged to her nephew. She also claimed that her nephew’s school fees would be deducted from the Joint Account by GIRO. She further claimed that she transferred $50,000 from her Joint Account to her Savings Account because she did not want to “implicate” her nephew in “criminal breach of trust”. She testified that when she deposited $50,000 into her Joint Account, she had told TSM that $40,000 out of this sum of $50,000 did not belong to her (as she had “borrowed” this sum from her nephew). She claimed that TSM had responded by telling her to go to the bank to withdraw $50,000 in cash and pass the cash to him. He would then issue a cheque to her for this sum. However, she did not do this as she had already resigned and did not want to work anymore.[^340] Quah’s testimony on the $50,000 cashier’s order is set out at **Annex B** to these grounds.

212    I did not give any weight to Quah’s evidence. I was aware that Counsel did put certain questions to TSM regarding a loan of $40,000 and the Joint Account. These questions and TSM’s forceful denials are set out:[^341]

> Q:    \[TSM\], in 2012, did you take a loan of $40,000 from \[Quah\]?

> A:    No.

> Q:    Okay. My instruction\[s\] are that you took a loan \[of\] $40,000 from \[Quah\] in 2012. Do you agree or disagree?

> **A:**      **I disagree.**

> Q:    And then sometime from February or March 2014 to July 2014, you told her that she could keep the monies received from payments made \[by EDS\] to set off against the monies that you owed her. Do you agree or disagree?

> **A:**      **There’s no such thing.**

> Q:    Can you turn me with to \[the bank statement for the Joint Account\]? Okay. My instructions are that this \[statement in respect of the Joint Account\] sets out the cash cheques which were issued by \[EDS\]. And the cash cheques were deposited into these accounts. Are you aware?

> **A:**      **I do not know.**

> Q:    Okay. My instructions are that you did see this \[bank statement for the Joint Account\] before.

> **A:**      **No. I’ve never seen it.**

> …

> Q:    \[TSM\], if you look at the 4th line from the bottom, the date of 11th June 2014? Next to it there is an amount of $50,000 and if you continue reading across the line to the last column, it says, “Cashier’s Order”. So my instructions are that \[Quah\] drew out a Cashier’s Order of $50,000 and she also printed out a copy of this bank account statement. And she showed you both the Cashier’s Order and \[the bank account statement\].

> **A:**      **There’s no such thing at all.**

> Q:    And my instructions are that you told her she can keep this $50,000 Cashier’s Order and you would take it that you no longer owed her money. Do you agree or disagree?

> **A:**      **There’s no such thing, no.**

> Q:    And my instructions are that on the copy of this document which she printed out \[_ie_, the bank account statement in respect of the Joint Account\]. Both you and her actually signed off on it. Do you agree or disagree?

> **A:**      **I do not know \[about this\].**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

213    There was, however, _no_ mention that the loan which Quah had purportedly extended to TSM, also included the $11,000 security deposit the Company allegedly required from Ho.[^342] It was also difficult to understand why Quah (an employee of the Company) had to extend a personal loan of $11,000 to TSM on behalf of a customer of the Company. In this regard, I bore in mind Ho’s evidence that Quah had _never_ informed him of the need for any additional “security deposit”:[^343]

> Q:    Okay. Let’s move on to another point. Do you recall that Madam Quah had spoken to you before about a security deposit that the company required from you? A security deposit in the amount of $11,000?

> A:    No.

> …

> Q:    Okay. Mr Ho, you said that you had placed a deposit for the diesel chip, right?

> A:    Yup, mmm.

> Q:    And that was in the amount of $900?

> A:    Yah, yes, mmm.

> …

> **Q:**      **Subsequently, did \[Quah\] communicate to you that the company needed you to place more money as deposit?**

> **A:**      **Uh, no**, all the while she handle my account then she say she know how to handle as I got ask her \[if\] I need to approach \[TSM\] but she say, don’t have to, she know how to handle with \[TSM\].

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

214    There was no reason for Ho to lie. Neither did Quah advance one.

215    There were another inconsistency in Quah’s evidence. In cross-examination and re-examination, she had testified that TSM had written certain words on a photocopy of the cashier’s order she had allegedly passed him.[^344] However, it was put to TSM that he had done so on the bank statement relating to her Joint Account (_viz_., a _different_ document) that she had _also_ supposedly passed him.[^345] In addition, it was only in re-examination that Quah said that she had a scanned copy of this cashier’s order (on which TSM had apparently written certain words) in her computer.[^346] She also failed to mention the existence of this scanned copy, when she claimed that she had receipts proving that she handed $451,400 in cash to TSM.[^347] The circumstances leading to Quah bringing the cashier’s order to TSM in the Office were also not raised in her examination-in-chief and TSM’s cross-examination. This included her alleged conversation with TSM on not wanting to implicate her nephew.[^348]

216    Looking at the evidence as a whole, I agreed with the Prosecution that Quah never had $50,000 to lend to TSM. Given that her two remaining accounts were both credit lines, there was no objective evidence that she had the funds to do so. This was simply a case of her transferring misappropriated monies that had accumulated in her Joint Account to her Savings Account.

#### Entrusted Monies distinct from cash TSM received from Quah

217    In examination-in-chief, TSM testified that Quah was responsible for depositing the cash she collected from the Company’s customers into the Company’s Account. However, he also said that Quah would pass him small sums of cash in the range of $200 to $400 (being cash payments she had collected from the Company’s customers) five to seven times a month between 2009 and 2014. When these sums accumulated to a few thousand dollars, he would issue a personal cheque to return the money to the Company (the “Cash for Personal Cheque Practice”). It was his evidence that Quah would inform him of the sums due to the Company. She also wrote the sums on his personal cheque (based on her records). TSM testified that Quah “would write everything on his cheque and then after she’s done, \[he\] would \[just\] sign the cheque, and pass it back to her”. She would then bring his cheque to the bank and deposit it into the Company’s Account.[^349]

218    According to TSM, this practice had been in place even before Quah joined the Company. It was adopted because it was “very troublesome” for small sums of cash to be deposited into the bank every time they were received. TSM testified that he had initially recorded the sums that Quah passed him in the first six to seven years after she joined the Company. He ceased doing so thereafter because he trusted Quah. He was asked how he then knew if the sums Quah wrote on his personal cheques were correct. He replied that he trusted Quah because she had been working for him “for so long”. His evidence on these aspects is set out below:[^350]

> Q:    Did you have any way of keeping track of how much cash you received from \[Quah\] every month in this manner?

> A:    I did not record.

> **Q:**      **How then would you know that the amount \[Quah\] filled in on \[your personal\] cheque was correct?**

> **A:**      **Because she had been working for me for so long, I trusted her.**

> Q:    Did you write down how much cash you received anywhere?

> A:    Initially…not long after \[Quah\] joined the company, I did record this in a notebook. So, every month if the amounts are correct, I would erase it.

> **Q:**      **And can you clarify what timeframe or what year you are referring to? You said initially, not long after \[Quah\] joined. And she joined in 2000?**

> **A:**      **For the first 6 to 7 years, after that I trusted her, so I stopped recording.**

> **Q:**      **To the best of your recollection, do you have records of the cash you received from \[Quah\] between 2009 and 2014?**

> **A:**      **I did not record in the later part, because I trusted her.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

219    TSM’s account of the Cash for Personal Cheque Practice was supported by the cheque registers in his personal chequebooks (collectively, “the Cheque Registers”), which were admitted into evidence (**P22**). These Cheque Registers contained a record of all the cheques issued from TSM’s personal account[^351], and included the details of several cheques that TSM had issued to the Company during the offending period. Among these cheques were two that were dated 18 February 2014 and 24 March 2014. Images of these cheques were also admitted into evidence (**P23** and **P24**), and further supported the existence of this practice. These images showed that both cheques had been issued to the Company, and corresponded to rows in the Cheque Registers where the words “Exchange Cash – Clbus” had been written.[^352]

220    According to TSM, only three persons had written in his chequebooks during the offending period: himself; Fion; and Quah. [^353] That said, Fion would not make any entries in respect of the Company because she was not involved in the Company’s work. Save for his signatures on these two cheques, it was TSM’s evidence that he did not write the dates, the payee (_ie_, the Company), and the sums stated. He was sure of this because he could not write English.[^354] Given TSM’s _unchallenged_ evidence that it was Quah who had filled in these details[^355], I found that it was Quah who had written the dates, payee (_ie_, the Company), and the sums stated on these personal cheques. Quah had also agreed in cross-examination that she wrote these sums on TSM’s personal cheques.[^356]

221    It was TSM’s evidence that he adopted the Cash for Personal Cheque Practice for _all_ the cash payments he received from Quah:[^357]

> Q:    And did you do this, exchanging cash for \[personal cheque\] for **all** the cash that \[Quah\] handed to you?

> A:    Yes.

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

222    It was hence TSM’s evidence that the personal cheques he issued to the Company _fully_ accounted for the cash payments he received from Quah.

223    Quah did _not_ challenge TSM’s evidence on the Cash for Personal Cheque Practice during his cross-examination. I noted that TSM’s evidence on the existence of this practice was also consistent with Fion’s evidence as to the existence of a similar practice at SINCL (which Quah did _not_ challenge as well).[^358]

224    However, when cross-examined, Quah denied that:[^359]

> (a)     all of the cash payments that TSM received from her were fully accounted for by way of the Cash for Personal Cheque Practice.

> (b)     the Entrusted Monies were distinct from the relevant sums stated in the Cheque Registers.

> (c)     the sums of cash recorded by TSM in the Cash Record Book was distinct from the Entrusted Monies.

225    In closing submissions, Counsel thus sought to link the Entrusted Monies and the relevant sums stated in the Cheque Registers:

> 18.    From 10 December 2009 to 24 March 2014, the total amount of cash which was recorded in \[the Cheque Registers as having been exchanged for \[personal\] cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\] was **S$542,980**. Of this sum, the total amount that was deposited into the \[Company’s Account\] as recorded in the bank statements of the \[Company’s Account\] was **S$525,259.40**. A table setting out the total amount of cash recorded in the \[Cheque Registers\], as having been exchanged for \[personal\] cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\], and the total sum that was deposited into the \[Company’s Account\] as recorded in the \[Company’s Account\] Statements, is annexed as **Annex C** to these Closing Submissions.

> …

> 69.    As stated in paragraph 18 above, the \[Cheque Registers\] demonstrate that from 10 December 2009 to 24 March 2014, at least **S$525,259.40** was accounted for by \[personal\] cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\]. Although TSM tried, unsuccessfully, to downplay the sums of cash that he received, the \[Cheque Registers\] corroborate \[Quah’s\] evidence that the sums received by TSM were “_not small amounts_”, and we further elaborate on this in paragraphs 73 to 74 below.

> …

> 73.    We highlight, again, that while TSM and \[Quah\] are in agreement that she handed cash to TSM, their respective positions on the amount of cash that was handed to TSM, are different. In this regard:

>> (1)    TSM had tried to downplay the sums of cash that had been collected by \[Quah\] and handed to him, by alleging in his testimony that (a) \[Quah\] would only collect small amounts such as “_3 to $400_”, and that (b) this only took place, at most, “_6 to 7 times_” in a month. This is incredulous, and inconsistent with the \[Cheque Registers\]. As stated in paragraph 18 above, the \[Cheque Registers\] demonstrate that from 10 December 2009 to 24 March 2014 (a period of about 55 months), at least **S$525,259.40** has been accounted for by cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\]. On average, therefore, \[Quah\] would have handed about S$10,000 each month to TSM. This is vastly inconsistent with TSM’s evidence that \[Quah\] would hand him, at the most, S$2,800 each month!

>> (2)    \[Quah\] has denied that it was only “_small amounts_” that were handed to TSM, and accounted for by cheques issued by TSM in favour of the \[Company’s Account\]. Her evidence is borne out by, and consistent with, the \[Cheque Registers\].

> 74.    It is apparent from the matters sets out in paragraph 73 above that TSM is an unreliable witness.

> 75.    The \[Cheque Registers\] are also incontrovertible evidence that cash from the Cash Collection Practice, Encashing Practice, and Cash Withdrawal Practice, was handed to TSM, and was accounted for by cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\]. In this regard:

>> (1)    \[Quah\] collected at least **S$210,007.66** from the Cash Collection Practice, and handed this to TSM. A table setting out the respective \[Clients\], the amount paid by \[them\] in cash which was collected by \[Quah\], and handed to TSM, is annexed as **Annex D** to these Closing Submissions.

>> (2)    \[Quah\] would have collected at least **S$34,114.66** from the Encashing Practice, and handed this to TSM. A table showing the cash that was collected from the Encashing Practice, and handed to TSM, is annexed as **Annex E** to these Closing Submissions.

>> (3)    Pursuant to the Cash Withdrawal Practice, \[Quah\] withdrew **S$452,400** and handed this, together with her “_personal money_” to TSM.

>> (4)    Further, of the cash handed to TSM by \[Quah\], the \[Cheque Registers\] demonstrate that from 10 December 2009 to 24 March 2014, at least the sum of S$525,259.40 was accounted for by cheques issued by TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\].

> \[emphasis in original\]

226    I did not find these submissions compelling. This was for three reasons.

##### Inaccurate conflation

227     First, I agreed with the Prosecution that this was an “inaccurate conflation of issues”.[^360] This was for two reasons.

TSM accounted for all cash received with personal cheques

228     One, it went against TSM’s _unchallenged_ evidence that he adopted the Cash for Personal Cheque Practice for _all_ the cash payments received from Quah. It was his evidence that the personal cheques he issued _fully_ accounted for these payments.

Entrusted Monies not banked into Company’s Account

229     Two, none of the Entrusted Monies had been banked into the Company’s Account. This was the _unchallenged_ evidence of the Special Auditor.[^361] Quah also admitted to this, twice, when cross-examined.[^362] The first occasion was at the outset of her cross-examination, when the Prosecution read out the sums stated in each charge:[^363]

> Q:    Now, Madam Quah, the amounts in the 5 charges against you have been read to you.

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And these contain the sums that you are alleged to have been entrusted with and misappropriated. And just to make sure that we’re on the same page, I’m going to repeat the sums in each charge to you. So for the 1st charge, you’re alleged to have been entrusted with $174,166.12. For the 2nd charge, you’re alleged to have been entrusted with $169,974.60. For the 3rd charge, you are alleged to have been entrusted with $221,172.91. For the 4th charge, you’re alleged to have been entrusted with $127,104.40. And finally, for the 5th charge, you are alleged to have been entrusted with $233,403.66.

> A:    What is the total amount?

> Q:    The total amount is in excess of $900,000, Madam Quah. And you have heard clients of Chin Lin testify in Court that they paid money to you for all the relevant invoices that have been adduced in evidence, agree?

> A:    I disagree.

> Q:    Are you saying that you did not hear their evidence, Madam Quah?

> A:    I agree that they said this in Court.

> Q:    And you heard this from Eric Ho, Lee Fee Kun, Teo Tai Joo, Tan Kok Chuan, Ku Aik Beng, and Tan Yong Tiong?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And you agree that their evidence in this respect that they paid you for these relevant invoices was not challenged?

> A:    I agree.

> …

> Q:    You have heard IO Norazman testify that the sums in the charges---the sums in the charges that we went through earlier were summations of transactions marked “1” and “2” in the \[Clients’ Customer Transactions Records\], you agree?

> A:    I agree.

> **Q:**      **And you have also heard \[the Special Auditor explain\] that the amounts marked “1” and “2” were amounts paid by customers that were not banked into \[the Company’s Account\].**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And in fact, you yourself agree that these amounts---the same amounts that we’ve been talking about from the start of my questioning were not banked into \[the Company’s Account\]?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

230    The second occasion was towards the end of the second day of her cross-examination, when she was referred to EDS’s Customer Transactions Record:[^364]

> Q:    Now, I want you to go back to \[EDS’s Customer Transactions Record\] and that is page 646 of the bundle. Are you there, Mdm. Quah?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And I’m just going to remind you that you confirmed earlier in your testimony that you made all the accounting entries that have circles in one and circles in two next to them.

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So I want you to focus on the second column from the right and that’s the column labelled, “Transaction Amount”. Do you see that, Mdm. Quah? Now, the negative figures under that column, they indicate that Chin Lin’s invoices had been paid, agree?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So, for example, if you look with me at the 4th figure---4th figure from the top of that column. That is negative 5,881.96.

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So this negative figure indicates that this amount, 5,881.96, have been paid by the client, correct?

> A:    Yes

> Q:    But you also agreed that these amounts were not banked into \[the Company’s Account\], correct?

> A:    I would need to look at the bank statement and the documents.

> **Q:**      **So you’ve agreed with me already, Mdm. Quah that A, you collected all the sums in the charges and B, they were not banked into \[the Company’s Account\]. So this is just one such sum which I’m now highlighting to you.**

> **A:**      **Yes. Because it’s not negative and there’s one OCBC cheque.**

> Q:    Yes, so you agree that this sum was paid by the client but not banked into the \[Company’s Account\]?

> A:    I cannot be sure because I do not know when the cash cheque---Eric Ho’s cash cheque was encashed unless I have the bank statement. I could tell you where this went to but if you look at this, two is debtor’s balance off set in…director’s loan account.

> **Q:**      **Now, Mdm Quah…before we go further, now, I just want you to focus on the question. So I’ve already explained to you that this is just one such sum which was not banked into the \[Company’s Account\] and this actually accords with your own evidence so I’m just telling you that now. And the \[Special Auditor\] also gave evidence that this was not banked into the \[Company’s Account\].**

> **A:**      **Alright.**

> **Q:**      **So can we agree that this sum $5,881.96 not banked into \[the Company’s Account\]?**

> **A:**      **Yes. Yes, because by the fact, that it’s number 2, it---it means that the debtors balance were offset in the director’s loan account, so…one can be sure that this did not go into the \[Company’s Account\].**

> **Q:**      **So on one hand, we have this account showing that all these negative amounts have been paid by clients, correct? All the negative figures.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And on the other hand, we are also in agreement that \[the Company’s Account bank\] statement shows that these amounts have not been banked in.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

231    Quah was not re-examined on these admissions. She also did not appear confused when she made these admissions. In closing submissions, however, Counsel argued that her admissions were based on a “misunderstanding”. Counsel contended that her admissions merely “acknowledge\[d\] that if the sums paid by the \[Clients\] were recorded…as being debited to the director’s loan account, \[then\] it could not \[also\] be debited to the…bank ledger”.[^365] In light of Quah’s clear admissions and the _unchallenged_ evidence of the Special Auditor[^366], I saw no merit to this argument. I agreed with the Prosecution that this “post-hoc explanation \[of a “misunderstanding” was\] an unmeritorious attempt to re-characterise \[Quah’s\] evidence”.[^367] In this regard, I considered – but rejected[^368] – Counsel’s submission that the Special Auditor’s conclusion that the Entrusted Monies were not deposited into the Company’s Account was “unsupported by the documentary evidence, unreliable, and simply cannot be taken at face value”.[^369] I set out the relevant paragraphs in Counsel’s submissions:

> 80.     Secondly, there are information gaps in \[the Special Auditor’s\] review. We explain as follows:

>> (1)    \[The Special Auditor\] has not, either in \[her conditioned statement\], or her testimony, testified that she was aware of the Cash Collection Practice, Encashing Practice, or Cash Withdrawal Practice.

>> (2)    There is no mention of whether \[the Special Auditor\] had considered the \[Cheque Registers\]. This is a glaring omission. It would be impossible to verify whether the cash from the Cash Collection Practice, Encashing Practice, and Cash Withdrawal Practice was handed to TSM, and subsequently accounted for by cheques issued to TSM, in favour of the \[Company’s Account\], without having reviewed the \[Cheque Registers\]!

> 81.     Thirdly, \[the Special Auditor’s\] crucial admissions during trial demonstrate that \[her conclusion\] simply cannot be taken at face value. In this regard:

>> (1)    \[The Special Auditor\] admitted that she did not even know that the sums paid by the \[Clients\] were accounted for in cash whether directly, or _via_ encashed cash cheques. Again, without having knowledge of this, it would be impossible to verify whether the cash from the Cash Collection Practice, Encashing Practice, and Cash Withdrawal Practice was accounted for by deposits into the \[Company’s Account\]…

>> (2)    \[The Special Auditor\] admitted that she could not “_establish if money received by the directors had been banked into the \[Company’s Account_”….

>> …

> 82.    \[The Special Auditor’s\] admissions that she did not notice that payments were made by \[the Clients\] in cash, and that she could not “establish if money received by the directors had been banked into the \[Company’s Account\], are crucial and significant admissions. The thrust of \[Quah’s\] case is that the cash from the Cash Collection Practice, the Encashing Practice, and the Cash Withdrawal Practice, was handed to TSM.

> \[emphasis in original\]

232    I rejected these submissions. They did not reflect the case that Quah advanced during the Special Auditor’s relatively brief cross-examination. In addition, they attempted to challenge – indirectly – the Directors’ unchallenged evidence that they had never borrowed money from the Company.[^370] In this regard, I agreed with the Prosecution’s reply to these submissions – which I reproduce below:

> 11.     Third, the Defence’s claim at \[80\] of their closing submissions that there were “information gaps” in \[the Special Auditor’s\] review is flawed. The Defence did not describe the purported “Cash Collection Practice”, “Encashing Practice” and “Cash Withdrawal Practice” to \[the Special Auditor\], let alone put their case to \[the Special Auditor\] that \[Quah\] had engaged in these purported practices. The Defence also did not offer \[the Special Auditor\] an opportunity to comment on how these practices would have an impact, if any, on the findings and conclusions of her special audit. The “Cash Collection Practice”, “Encashing Practice” and “Cash Withdrawal Practice” \[were\] terms that the Defence introduced for the first time in their closing submissions.

> 12.    The Defence’s claim at \[80(2)\] of their closing submissions that \[the Special Auditor\] had not considered the \[Cheque Registers\] is also flawed. The Defence did not put their case regarding the \[Cheque Registers\] to \[the Special Auditor\], and cannot now belatedly seek to criticise her evidence on that basis.

> 13.    In addition, the Defence did not apply to recall \[the Special Auditor\] to cross-examine her _after_ the \[Cheque Registers\] had been admitted into evidence.

> 14.     Fourth, the Defence attempts to rely on \[the Special Auditor’s\] “admission” that she could not establish if money received by the \[Directors\] had been banked into the \[Company’s Account\] in support of their submission that \[the Special Auditor’s conclusion\] “cannot be taken at face value”. The Defence’s argument is a non-starter.

> 15.    The \[Directors of the Company, TSM, LEC, and NES\] have each _directly_ testified that they had never loaned money from \[the Company\] in the first place…Each \[had\] also testified as to his limited proficiency in English, and each \[had\] explained that he would sign the documents that \[Quah\] handed him based on what \[Quah had explained to him\]. The Defence cannot \[now belatedly\] challenge the veracity, weight and internal consistency of this direct evidence by attacking \[the Special Auditor’s\] evidence.

##### Belated attempt to link Entrusted Monies & Cheque Registers

233     Second, this attempt to link the Entrusted Monies and the relevant sums in the Cheque Registers was a very belated one. It also encompassed yet another fresh claim, which was not raised during TSM’s cross-examination. As the Prosecution pointed out:[^371]

> \[Quah\] never mentioned the \[Cheque Registers\] in \[any of\] her \[12\] police statements or \[in\] her evidence-in-chief. It was only \[at the tail end of her\] cross-examination that she belatedly attempted to claim that the \[Cheque Registers\] were related to the \[Entrusted Monies\]. It was **_never_** her defence that she handed the \[Entrusted Monies\] to TSM **and** that she would assist him to write personal cheques to the \[Company’s Account\] for _parts_ of these \[Entrusted Monies\]. Moreover, \[Quah\] herself agreed that she assisted with filling in the relevant cheques; she therefore must have known of the existence of the \[Cheque Registers\] long before they were adduced in evidence \[during the trial\], and _yet_ not raised them in her defence…

> \[emphasis added in original\]

##### No explanation for illogical & roundabout process

234     Third, it was difficult to understand why Quah (or any reasonable person) would engage in a roundabout process to deposit the cash from the cash cheques she collected into the Company’s Account. As the Prosecution noted:[^372]

> Taken at its highest, \[Quah’s\] defence is that that she handed over all of the \[Entrusted Monies\] in cash to TSM and/or…supplemented as necessary with her personal money. \[But, she\] offered no explanation for why she would engage in a protracted \[and circuitous\] practice of encashing \[cash\] cheques or depositing them into her \[three personal bank accounts\] and withdrawing the \[cash corresponding to these cash cheques\], handing the cash sums to TSM, and _then_ assisting him to write personal cheques back to the \[Company’s Account\]. She could have simply and rightly deposited the relevant \[cash\] cheques \[into the Company’s Account\] to begin with…

> \[emphasis in original\]

235    Quah never testified that TSM told her to engage in such an illogical process.

##### Quantum of sums in Cheque Registers irrelevant

236    Counsel argued that TSM was an “unreliable witness” because he had “tried to downplay the sums of cash” he received from Quah.[^373] I saw no merit to this. TSM never denied the sums stated in the Cheque Registers, and thus never “downplayed” them. It was also not his evidence that Quah “would hand him, at the most, S$2,800 each month”. More importantly, this argument missed the point. The key issue was whether the Entrusted Monies were distinct from the cash payments that TSM received from Quah, and _not_ their quantum. I therefore saw no reason not to give full weight to TSM’s evidence on the Cash for Personal Cheques Practice.[^374] I agreed with the Prosecution that the cash payments that TSM received from Quah were “entirely accounted for and separate from the \[Entrusted Monies\] which \[were\] the subject of the charges”.[^375] This thus meant that Quah never passed TSM the cash portion of the Entrusted Monies.

#### No explanation for what happened to remainder of Entrusted Monies

237     **Annex C** to these grounds is a breakdown of the Entrusted Monies. I have already considered, but rejected, Quah’s evidence in relation to her Compilation and the Summation[^376]. This was on the cash cheques she admitted to collecting from EDS, Win Tran and Time-Flex – which she did not deposit into the Company’s Account.

238    The Summation related, however, to only a sum of $569,788.89. This was but a portion of the Entrusted Monies. The remaining portion of the Entrusted Monies (amounting to a total of $350,032.80) comprised:

> (a)     cash payments (amounting to a total of $210,007.66) that Quah admitted to collecting from:

>> (i)       Tan Kok Chuan;

>> (ii)       Teo Tai Joo;

>> (iii)       Ku Aik Beng;

>> (iv)       Sin Kook Seng Enterprise; and

>> (v)       EDS.

> (b)     22 cheques (for a total sum of $140,025.14) that Quah admitted to collecting from:

>> (i)       Tan Yong Tiong (Sin Kook Seng Enterprise): one cash cheque;

>> (ii)       EDS: 18 cheques;

>> (iii)       Win Tran: two cheques; and

>> (iv)       Ho: one cheque.

239    Quah did not bank _any_ of this remaining portion of the Entrusted Monies into the Company’s Account. I had earlier found that the cash portion of the Entrusted Monies were distinct from the cash payments that TSM received from Quah (which were fully accounted for by TSM’s Cash for Personal Cheque Practice).[^377] Quah therefore never passed this cash portion of the Entrusted Monies to TSM. It was also Ho’s unchallenged evidence that he paid the Company by way of cash cheques only.[^378] This therefore meant that all 22 cheques that Quah collected (and which made up the remaining portion of the Entrusted Monies[^379]) were _cash_ cheques. Against this backdrop, I noted that Quah did not put forth any evidence in examination-in-chief on this remaining portion of the Entrusted Monies (unlike her Compilation). As the Prosecution noted, the “implicit admission \[therefore was\] that \[Quah was\] unable and/or unwilling to account for \[this remaining portion of the Entrusted Monies\]”.[^380]

240    That said, Counsel asserted in closing submissions that:

> 75.    …

>> (1)    \[Quah\] collected at least **S$210,007.66** from the Cash Collection Practice, and handed this to TSM. A table setting out the respective \[Clients\], the amount paid by \[them\] in cash which was collected by \[Quah\], and handed to TSM, is annexed as **Annex D** to these Closing Submissions.

> \[emphasis in original\]

241    But, as the Prosecution correctly observed, Quah “never testified that she had handed over all the sums \[stated\] in Annex D \[of the Defence’s Closing Submissions\] to TSM in her evidence-in-chief”.[^381] “Annex D” was also not put before TSM during his cross-examination. It only first appeared in Counsel’s closing submissions. The rule in _Browne v Dunn_[^382] was hence engaged. As reiterated by the Court of Appeal in _Harven a/l Segar v PP_[^383], the effect of the rule is that:

> …\[w\]here a submission is going to be made about a witness or the evidence given by the witness which is of such a nature and of such importance that it ought fairly to have been put to the witness to give him the opportunity to meet that submission, to counter it or to explain himself, then if it has not been so put, the party concerned will not be allowed to make that submission.

242    I therefore did not give any weight to Counsel’s submission on “Annex D”.

#### Quah sought cash and/or cash cheques from Clients

243    In examination-in-chief:[^384]

> (a)     Tan Kok Chuan testified that Quah had suggested that he pay the Company in cash.

> (b)     Lee (from Time-Flex) testified that Quah had asked her to issue cash cheques “so that her TSM \[could\] bank in the cheque at any time”.

> (c)     Ho (from EDS and Win Tran) testified that Quah had asked him to pay the Company using cash cheques.

244    In cross-examination, the Special Auditor testified that TSM had informed her and Heng at the meeting before the special audit that he had learnt from Ho that:[^385]

> …EDS was issuing…cash cheques…for payment of outstanding invoices rather than…issuing…crossed cheques payable to \[the Company\].

245    Quah did not challenge these aspects of the evidence. I was aware that she had testified that TSM wanted her to collect cash cheques from:[^386]

> (a)     Time-Flex as it had cash flow problems; and

> (b)     EDS “to make it more convenient for \[TSM\] to collect the cash.”

246    But, this was never put to TSM – even though Counsel stated that it was a fact that Quah intended to rely on.[^387]

247    In examination-in-chief, Ho testified that Quah would sometimes[^388] ask if he had “hard cash” after he had _already_ passed her a cash cheque to pay the Company. If he did, she would ask to “exchange” his cash cheque for cash. She would then return the cash cheque to him after receiving the equivalent amount of cash from Ho.[^389] In this regard, the Prosecution referred Ho to a cash cheque (**P6**) issued from Win Tran’s account.[^390] This cheque was dated 15 April 2011 and for the sum of $2,750. It was not disputed that the Company never received this sum. It was Ho’s evidence that Quah had returned this cheque to him when he passed her $2,750 in cash. According to Ho, he had initially passed Quah a signed cheque with just the figure of $2,750 typed on it. When Quah returned the cheque to him after he had passed her $2,750 in cash, she had already written the date and the word “cash” in the payee section of the cheque. I set out Ho’s evidence:[^391]

> Q:    But this cheque was supposed to be for payment for diesel?

> A:    Yes. As \[Quah\] request me to pass her the hard cash in order to give back my cheque.

> **Q:**      **Okay. So this was an instance where \[Quah\] returned the cheque to you, is that correct?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **So who requested this? Did you request the return of the cheque or did she \[?\]**

> **A:**      **She call me.**

> **Q:**      **\[A\]nd what did \[Quah\] tell you?**

> **A:**      **She told me that “Do you have hard cash?” I say “Have”. So, she asked me to withdraw the $2,750 and pass to her. At the same time, \[she\] will return the cheque to me.**

> Q:    Now, earlier you explained that when you gave the cheque to \[Quah\] you had only filled in your signature and the amount. When the cheque was returned to you, what else was filled in?

> A:    Before I pass to \[Quah\] the cheque it’s blank cheque…I only sign and write the figure amount. When the day \[she\] call me for the hard cash, I passed her the hard cash, she passed me back the cheque, I return by her, the cheque and the cross and the date itself.

> **Q:**      **So just to make sure that I’ve got that correctly, you said that when she returned it to you, there was the word cash, the cross and the date.**

> **A:**      **Yah.**

> Q:    What about the back of the cheque?

> A:    No, the back is written by me.

> Q:    And what did you do with the cheque after you had filled in the details on the back?

> A:    I deposit to my wife account.

> Q:    And to confirm, did you give the equivalent sum in cash to \[Quah\]? So $2,750?

> A:    Yah.

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

248    In cross-examination, Ho denied initiating the return of this cheque to Quah. He reiterated that it was Quah who had called him to ask for cash in return for this cheque:[^392]

> Q:    Okay. Okay, can you take up P6? P6 is a cheque image for the sum of $2,750...Okay earlier in your evidence, you said that \[Quah\] had asked you for cash to return this cheque to you?

> A:    Yes.

> **Q:**      **Okay. Were you the one who first contacted \[Quah\] to ask for a return of this cheque?**

> **A:**      **Uh, no \[she\] call me to meet…her at…Bukit Batok Central.**

> Q:    Okay. I put my instructions to you, okay? My instructions are that, for this cheque, you were the one who contacted her first to ask for this cheque to be returned, you can agree, disagree or you can say…you can’t remember.

> A:    \[D\]isagree.

> Q:    …Okay. So she then told you that she can return this cheque to you but first you have to give her cash, so that she can use it as your payment to the company?

> A:    In---yah.

> Q:    So, that’s a yes?

> A:    Yes.

> **Q:**      **Okay. Let’s just clarify because, we are trying to determine…who initiated the return of this cheque, okay? So my instructions are that, you asked first for this cheque to be returned and then she asked you for the cash, so that, the cheque can be returned to you?**

> **A:**      **No, it’s like…\[she\] asked me to pay cash to her at the same time, give back the cheque to me.**

> Q:    Yes. So that’s what eventually happened, right?

> A:    Yes.

> **Q:**      **So what we…are trying to understand is who initiated this event that had occurred, because my instructions are that, you first contacted Madam Quah to ask for this cheque to be returned.**

> **A:**      **Of course, she is the one who call me…is she \[who\] need hard cash…**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

249    I accepted Ho’s evidence. He had no reason to lie. There was no need for him to initiate the return of this cheque and pay cash to Quah, when he had (essentially) already passed her a cheque for this same sum. That Quah had written the word “cash” in the payee section of the cheque (when she returned the cheque to Ho) was not disputed. There was hence no reason why Quah could not have deposited this cheque into the Company’s Account (or any of her personal bank accounts, as she claimed TSM instructed her to). I found that it was Quah who initiated the return of this cheque in exchange for cash on hand – which she could more easily, and did in fact, misappropriate. It was of not fortuitous that the modes of payment Quah suggested/dictated[^393] (cash and cash cheques) were those that were misappropriated.

#### Quah manipulated accounting records to hide misappropriation

250    The Company never cancelled or voided concluded sales transactions with its customers.[^394] Quah confirmed this as well:[^395]

> **Q:**      **…Now, Mdm Quah, in your long experience with \[the Company\], has any customer ever cancelled a sales transaction?**

> **A:**      **No.**

> Q:    So I just want to be clear about this point because \[the Company\] sells diesel, right?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    So in your experience, has anyone ever pumped diesel into their vehicle \[and\] then left and then came back and ask\[ed\] for a refund?

> A:    No.

> **Q:**      **Has anyone ever tried to return the diesel pump\[ed\] into their vehicle?**

> **A:**      **It’s not possible.**

> **Q:**      **So the answer is no?**

> **A:**      **No.**

> **Q:**      **So definitely no cancelled sales transactions?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

251    The accounting entries corresponding to the Missing Payments debited to the “OTHER INCOME” account (marked on the Clients’ Customer Transactions Records) were therefore false. This was because they suggested that the Company had cancelled concluded sales transactions with the Clients.[^396] Quah also admitted that these entries did not reflect the true state of affairs:[^397]

> Q:    And in fact, you agreed with me earlier that no customer of \[the Company\] had cancelled a completed sales transaction. Yes or no?

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    In fact, you agreed that it’s not possible.

> A:    It’s not possible. After you pumped the diesel, it’s not possible to cancel.

> **Q:**      **So the entries marked one, they don’t reflect the true state of affairs, correct?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **Because there were, in fact, no cancelled sales transaction.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

252    The Directors never borrowed money from the Company.[^398] The accounting entries corresponding to the Missing Payments debited to the “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” account (marked on the Clients’ Customer Transactions Records) were therefore _also_ false – because they suggested that the Directors had received these payments (and not the Company) and therefore owed these sums to the Company.[^399]

253    Quah had made _all_ of these incriminating entries on ACCPAC.

254    When cross-examined, Quah claimed that TSM had instructed her to make these entries. I noted that this was somewhat consistent[^400] with her examination-in-chief, where she said that she had to meet TSM on the third day of every month for him to review the invoices she had prepared and the Clients’ Customer Transactions Records.[^401] Referring to the accounting entries marked on the Clients’ Customer Transactions Records), she claimed that TSM had told her sometime in 2009 during their monthly meetings[^402] that he did “not want to put \[certain\] sale figure\[s\] into the sales account, but “want\[ed\] \[her\] to transfer \[these figures\] to \[other\] income.”[^403] She said that she did as TSM directed. However, she also claimed that she did tell TSM that she did not agree with this practice. She said that TSM responded that “\[she\] was only an employee \[and\] \[h\]e wanted to distribute these monies to the other bosses, so he asked \[her\] to do as \[told\].”[^404]

255    However, TSM denied having discussions with Quah where he would review the general ledgers of the Company (which included the “OTHER INCOME” and “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” ledgers[^405]). He also forcefully testified that he had never seen the Clients’ Customer Transactions Records before:[^406]

> Q:    \[TSM\], tab 8 to tab 13 are the company’s customer transaction\[s\] \[record\]. For tab 8, it is for \[EDS\] and you can see that name at the top of the documents. Okay, my instructions are that on the 3rd day of every month, this document would have been reviewed by you?

> A:    No.

> Q:    If you turn with me to tab 9, this is the customer transactions record for Sin K\[oon\] Seng Enterprise. And on the discussion on the 3rd day of every month, you would have reviewed this document as well.

> A:    No.

> Q:    Let’s turn to tab 10. Tab 10 is the customer transactions record for \[Time-Flex\]. On the 3rd day of every month, at the discussion that you have with \[Quah\], you would also have reviewed this document?

> **A:**      **I’ve never seen these things. So even if you ask about the rest, \[my\] answer will be the same. There’s no need to ask so many \[questions\].**

> Q:    Now, let’s look at tab 11, tab 12, and tab 13. These are the customer transactions records for Teo Tai Joo, Tan Kok Chuan, and Ku Aik Beng respectively. So my instructions are that at the discussion on the 3rd day of every month, you would have also reviewed these documents?

> **A:**      **Just now I have said never...so…no matter how much you ask, it’s still no.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

256    TSM also denied that he would instruct Quah to:[^407]

> (a)     reverse customer payments that he selected into the “OTHER INCOME” ledger; and

> (b)     record customer payments that he selected under the “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” ledger.

257    TSM further denied that Quah had expressed her discomfort with these alleged practices. I set out his evidence in cross-examination:[^408]

> **Q:**      **And I put it to you \[that\] at this discussion on the 3rd day of every month, you would also review the general ledgers of the company.**

> **A:**      **No.**

> **Q:**      **…You would then instruct \[Quah\] to reverse payments from customers that you select\[ed\] into the general ledger of other income? Okay, I’ll repeat the question again**.

> DPP:  Your Honour, apologies. Just for clarity, is my learned friend referring to documents that have been admitted? If so could we just have the reference? Is he referring to AB38 and AB39?

> DC:    Your Honour, my instructions are that the general ledger as a whole and if Your Honour recalls \[when\] the auditors gave their evidence – general ledgers actually have different accounts. So my instructions are that the entire set was discussed at the meeting which I’m putting to \[TSM\] now.

> DPP:  Grateful to my learned friend.

> **A:**      **There’s no such thing ever.**

> **Q:**      **And you would have also selected certain customer payments to be recorded under director’s loan account instead?**

> **A:**      **No, I disagree. I’ve never known this.**

> **…**

> **Q:**      **And my instructions are that when \[Quah\] told you that she was not comfortable with this practice, you told her that she was only an employee?**

> **A:**      **There’s no such --- there’s never such thing.**

> **Q:**      **And you told her to just do as you had instructed her. And the monies were for you to go and deal with the other directors.**

> **A:**      **There’s no such thing. Can I say something? My mistake was that I trusted her too much. If I had not gone for the heart surgery, this wouldn’t have happened. So no matter how much you asked me now, there’s no meaning to this.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

258    I accepted TSM’s evidence. I also disbelieved Quah’s account, as it was incredible in light of my findings that:

> (a)     TSM’s proficiency in the English language (the language used in ACCPAC) was very limited[^409]; and

> (b)     TSM did not know how to use a computer or operate ACCPAC.[^410]

259    I set out Quah’s unbelievable account, for its incredulity to be appreciated:[^411]

> Q:    …Now, Mdm Quah, when you refer to other income and director’s loan ledgers in these proceedings, you’ve actually been referring to those terms in English \[when you testify in Court\], you agree?

> …

> A:    Yes.

> Q:    And that’s because you \[are\] not very sure what these words are in Mandarin, you agree?

> A:    I’m not sure.

> …

> Q:    Now, you agree that \[TSM\] would have given you instructions, if any, in Mandarin.

> A:    No.

> **Q:**      **So you are saying that \[TSM\] knew how to refer to “other income” and “director’s loan ledger” in English?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **I suggest \[to\] you, this is highly improbable given \[TSM’s\] limited English capacity.**

> **A:**      **I disagree.**

> Q:    Now, we are agreed on the fact that all one\[s\] and \[twos\] in \[the Customer Transactions Record of each Client\], all these are amount not banked into the \[Company’s Account\]?

> A:    Yes.

> **Q:**      **It must follow that if \[TSM\] had to instruct you which entries to mark as one and two, he had to do the following. Step 1, he would have to access ACCPAC.**

> **A:**      **Yes…and he did.**

> **Q:**      **Step 2, he would have to confirm which sums paid had not been banked into \[the Company’s Account\].**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And step 3, he would have to decide which of these entries to mark as one and two.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **In other words, he would have to decide which entries to reverse in other income?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And which entries to debit to the director’s loan accounts? Just yes or no, please, Mdm Quah.**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> **Q:**      **And this is despite the fact that \[TSM\] has given evidence that he did not even check the \[Company’s Account\].**

> A:    Is that even possible?

> Q:    You have heard his evidence, have you not, Mdm Quah?

> A:    I did.

> **Q:**      **And you have also heard his evidence that he did not know how to use ACCPAC?**

> **A:**      **I did.**

> **Q:**      **So your evidence, Mdm Quah, I’m giving you a chance to confirm, is that \[TSM\], a Primary 3-level educated man, \[who\] does not know how to turn on a computer, told you to do all of these?**

> **A:**      **Yes.**

> Q:    I suggest to you that this is –

> A:    He knows.

> Q:    incredible.

> A:    I disagree.

> Q:    So I ask you to confirm one more time for the record, your Defence is, basically, now that \[TSM\] was lying in Court.

> A:    Yes.

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

260    Having reviewed the totality of the evidence, I agreed with the Prosecution that the irresistible inference was that Quah independently and unilaterally manipulated the accounting records to conceal her dishonest misappropriation of the Entrusted Monies. This evidenced her dishonesty.[^412] As the Prosecution forcefully argued:

> 46    …

>> (c)    \[T\]he accounting entries on ACCPAC which correspond to the \[Entrusted Monies\] \[did\] not reflect the true state of affairs. None of the relevant sales transactions had been cancelled or refunded. None of the relevant directors (TSM, LEC and NES) had loaned money from \[the Company\]. Further, TSM did not even know to use ACCPAC. It is incredible to suggest that TSM had instructed \[Quah\] to manipulate the accounting entries on ACCPAC in a relatively sophisticated manner when he had no English proficiency and could not even operate a computer. The only logical conclusion is that \[Quah\] had independently manipulated the accounting entries to avoid detection.

261    In reply submissions, Counsel argued that the Prosecution was wrong in this submission.[^413] Counsel’s arguments were set out in detail in his closing submissions. The relevant extracts appear below:

> 119.  \[The Audit Firm\] was aware of the \[irregular entries corresponding to the Missing Payments debited to the “OTHER INCOME” account and the “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” account\]. In the course of \[preparing\] the Audited Accounts, \[the Audit Firm\] reviewed the general ledgers of \[the Company\], including the \[“OTHER INCOME” and “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” accounting ledgers[^414]\]. This was confirmed by \[Heng\] explicitly. The relevant extract \[from Heng’s cross-examination\] is as follows:[^415]

>> Q:    So, in addition to the management accounts, your staff would have also taken a look at the ---at the least, the \[“OTHER INCOME” and “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” accounting ledgers\], right?

>> A:    Yes.

> …

> 124.  \[T\]he documentary evidence is incontrovertible that TSM, LEC, and NES, were aware of the \[irregular entries corresponding to the Missing Payments debited to the “OTHER INCOME” account and the “AMOUNT OWING BY DIRECTORS” account\]. In this regard:

>> (1)    The \[Audited Accounts of the Company for the financial years ending on 30 June 2011, 30 June 2012, 30 June 2013, and 30 June 2014\] were prepared by \[the Audit Firm\], which signed off on each of the Audited Accounts.

>> (2)    TSM signed on each of these \[Audited Accounts\], stating that these represented a “_true and fair view of the state of affairs of \[the Company\]_”.

>> (3)    Further, for the financial years ended 30 June 2013 and 30 June 2014, TSM, LEC, and NES each verified the amount owing by them to \[the Company\]. These Audit Verification Letters were each counter-signed by another director, and confirmed by the directors from whom the money was owing…

> \[emphasis in original\]

262    I reiterate my findings that:[^416]

> (a)     Quah failed to explain the contents and significance of the audit verifications she gave the Directors to sign.

> (b)     the Directors trusted Quah when they signed these verifications.

263    I therefore did not think that the mere fact that the Directors signed the audit verifications was “incontrovertible” evidence that they were in fact aware of the irregular entries on ACCPAC. Neither were the Audited Accounts (on which the verifications were based) such evidence. As Heng explained, the irregularities discovered during the special audit were not detected during the general audits because Quah had entered the figures into the accounting records “like any other ordinary figure” and the “accounting records \[were\] full of figures”. Unless a “very detailed” and directed check was done, one was “not likely” to uncover anything. I set out Heng’s evidence:[^417]

> Q:    Looking at these \[irregular\] entries \[marked\] 1 and 2…why were these not flagged out in the annual \[general\] audit\[s\] of \[the Company\]?

> A:    \[U\]nder normal audit procedures, we did not detect these matters.

> Q:    Can you explain why these matters were not detected?

> A:    Because…those figures \[had been\] enter\[ed\] into the book like any other ordinary figure, and the accounting records \[were\] full of figure\[s\]. Unless, you do a very detailed \[directed check\], you are not likely to be able to find out anything.

264    In addition, Quah did not challenge TSM’s evidence on Heng’s explanation as to why the irregularities were not detected during the general audits. According to TSM, Heng had told him that “he would just pick and choose, selectively check. If there had been problems, \[and Quah\] had given him some explanation, he would let it off and not probe further”:[^418]

> Q:    So \[before LEC lodged the Company’s Police Report\], what did \[the Audit Firm\] give you?

> A:    \[The Audit Firm\] told us that the accounts were not right.

> Q:    And did they say what was not right about it?

> A:    He said there were a lot of discrepancies in the accounts that he has checked.

> Q:    Who from \[the Audit Firm\] told you that?

> A:    \[Heng\] himself.

> **Q:**      **And did you then ask \[Heng\] why these discrepancies were not picked up earlier?**

> **A:**      **I did ask \[Heng\], “You were…checking the accounts, yet how can you not know that….you have been checking for such a long time and you didn’t even know that the accounts were wrong?” So \[Heng\] said that he…would just pick and choose, selectively check. If there had been problems, if \[Quah\] had given him some explanation, he would let it off and not probe further.**

> \[emphasis added in bold\]

265    In these circumstances, I agreed with the Prosecution that Quah:[^419]

> …was in fact initially successful \[in hiding her misappropriation of the Entrusted Monies\], given that the discrepancies were not picked up in the general audits between 2009 and 2014, and only came to light after she…left \[the Company\] and \[the\] special audit was commissioned.

### Red herrings

266    During the course of the trial, Quah alleged that TSM:

> (a)     had terminated her employment because:[^420]

>> (i)       he had found out that she was preparing a document that recorded information of cheques issued from the Company’s Account to him (the “MBB Cheques Document”).[^421]

>> (ii)       she had made a police report against him alleging sexual harassment.[^422]

> (b)     had directed LEC to make the Company’s Police Report as he “bore a grudge”[^423] against her.

267    TSM denied these allegations. He also testified that he had never seen the MBB Cheques Document before.[^424] In any event, I found these allegations irrelevant to Quah’s criminal liability. I now elaborate.

#### MBB Cheques Document not related to Quah’s charges

268    Quah had first produced the MBB Cheques Document when her first investigation statement was recorded.[^425] However, she confirmed in her fourth investigation statement[^426] that it had nothing to do with the sums that were the subject of the charges against her (_viz_., the Entrusted Monies):

>   
| 

Q18?

 | 

Can I confirm that the \[MBB Cheques Document relates to\] a separate issue and not the missing cash the Police are investigating?

 |
| 

Answer:

 | 

**I confirmed that the \[MBB Cheques Document\] I produced had got nothing to do with the sum of S$900,000 that Police are investigating.** My purpose of producing this document \[is\] to show…the Police that \[TSM\] also took company money[^427] without the knowledge of the 3 other directors.

 |
| 

\[emphasis added in bold\]

 |

  
  

#### No allegation that TSM framed Quah after police report

269    In her second police report, Quah had alleged that TSM had started to accuse her of misusing the Company funds after she lodged her police report alleging sexual harassment.[^428] Her case at trial was, however, different. During the trial, she alleged that TSM terminated her employment because of her police report alleging sexual harassment. It was therefore not her case at trial that TSM had framed her because of this report. Indeed, this line of questioning was not pursued at trial. In any event, I did not place any weight on this police report in assessing TSM’s credibility[^429] – given that no further action was taken against TSM in respect of Quah’s allegations.[^430]

#### Audit Firm & lawyers suggested Company file police report

270    There was no merit in Quah’s assertion that TSM had directed LEC to make the Company’s Police Report as he “bore a grudge” against her. In examination-in-chief, TSM was asked about the circumstances leading to the Company’s Police Report. He testified that the Company had employed someone new to take over the accounts after Quah’s departure. This person had said that he was not able to do so, and asked TSM what to do. As TSM did “not know about the accounts”, he instructed the Audit Firm to check. TSM was then informed at a subsequent meeting with Heng that nearly a million dollars was missing. Heng told him to report the matter to the police and to engage a lawyer to help him handle the matter.[^431] TSM’s evidence was not challenged. It was also consistent with LEC’s and Fion’s evidence (which was not challenged as well) that it was the Audit Firm that told the Directors to report the Company’s accounting irregularities to the police.[^432]

271    In cross-examination, TSM denied that the Audit Firm’s auditors spoke to him in the course of their general audits about the records in the Company’s general ledger.[^433] He also explained why he did not make an earlier complaint to the Audit Firm or the police (which I accepted):[^434]

> Q:    And the fact of the matter was that you were keeping track of customer’s payments and you were keeping track of the monies actually received by the \[C\]ompany. And that is why you have never \[made\] any complaint to the police or the auditors, do you agree?

> A:    But **when I check you must know what I checked. I only checked that to make sure that these customers are not owing money for too long.** Because if the debts \[are\] for more than 2 or 3 months then…I must chase after them …if not I won’t have enough money to make payment \[to the diesel company\]. So I cannot allow payment to be dragged on for too long.

> \[emphasis added in bold\]
